## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillations (classical mechanics)
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the equation of motion includes nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), possibly nonlinear damping (functions of v), and potentially external driving (functions of t). The relationship dv/dt = f(x, v, t) represents Newton's second law with various nonlinear force contributions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- General polynomial restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (polynomial force with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry about equilibrium; even powers (x**2) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms (c*v) represent energy dissipation or injection; sign determines damping vs. anti-damping
- Position-velocity coupling terms (x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillators like van der Pol
- Periodic time-dependent terms sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicate external driving forces; their frequency relative to natural frequency determines resonance behavior
- Cubic position terms (x**3) with same sign as linear term indicate hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring (Duffing classification)
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved (if also no velocity terms) or dissipated
- Products of position powers and velocity (x**n * v) arise from nonlinear damping mechanisms where dissipation depends on displacement amplitude
- Time-modulated position terms x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric excitation, which can lead to parametric resonance at specific frequency ratios

Wait — could `(c + v)**c` somehow produce `|v|^(1/3)`? No, not generally.

Let me reconsider whether the GT truly requires `|v|`. The exponent is 1/3. If v represents a physical quantity that's always non-negative (like speed), then `v**(1/3) = |v|**(1/3)` and the distinction doesn't matter.
